  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7841df0a-6df6-432e-a251-e64e9b57e39d'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer14744235793327283783">As the daughter of a meth dealer, Wavy knows not to trust people, not even her own parents. Struggling to raise her little brother, eight-year-old Wavy is the only responsible "adult" around. She finds peace in the starry Midwestern night sky above the fields behind her house. One night everything changes when she witnesses one of her father's thugs, Kellen, a tattooed ex-</span>
  <span id="freeText14744235793327283783" style="display:none">As the daughter of a meth dealer, Wavy knows not to trust people, not even her own parents. Struggling to raise her little brother, eight-year-old Wavy is the only responsible "adult" around. She finds peace in the starry Midwestern night sky above the fields behind her house. One night everything changes when she witnesses one of her father's thugs, Kellen, a tattooed ex-con with a heart of gold, wreck his motorcycle. What follows is a powerful and shocking love story between two unlikely people that asks tough questions, reminding us of all the ugly and wonderful things that life has to offer.</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1730145556?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" href="/user/show/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake">Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29480865-all-the-ugly-and-wonderful-things">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=favorite-couple">favorite-couple</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=loved-you-since-childhood">loved-you-since-childhood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=gives-good-grovel">gives-good-grovel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=age-gap">age-gap</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1730145556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1331426535295902666"><b>4.5 Stars <br/><br/><i>"She is just as real as I am."</i></b><br/><br/>^^^That was my favorite line and moment in a book that was filled with more than a few touching lines and moments. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471579261i/20074998.jpg' width='350' height='219' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Before I say anything, let's address the large-trunked mammal who hath set his fat ass in the middle of this ugly and wonderful room. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471577478i/20074795.jpg' width='460' height='460' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Unless you live in a faraway goodreads cave (which I am totally not knocking, faraway caves are legit comfy hangouts) you have probably heard that the H/h in this book first...get involved...when they are 13 and</span>
  <span id="freeText1331426535295902666" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Stars <br><br><i>"She is just as real as I am."</i></b><br><br>^^^That was my favorite line and moment in a book that was filled with more than a few touching lines and moments. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471579261i/20074998.jpg" width="350" height="219" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Before I say anything, let's address the large-trunked mammal who hath set his fat ass in the middle of this ugly and wonderful room. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471577478i/20074795.jpg" width="460" height="460" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Unless you live in a faraway goodreads cave (which I am totally not knocking, faraway caves are legit comfy hangouts) you have probably heard that the H/h in this book first...get involved...when they are 13 and 24/5, respectively. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455572216ra/18120666.gif" width="500" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, this is a HUGE problem for some readers on a moral/comfort/ick-factor/whatever level and I totally respect that. <br><br><u>I don't presume to change people's minds and I'm not here to try. </u><br><br>We all believe, prefer and/or are comfortable/uncomfortable with different things. <br><br>And I'm down with that. <br><br>Some people can read about animals being slaughtered and I can't even read about one being left in a hot car for five minutes. <br><br>Others can't stand violence of any kind and I can read about torture and disembowelment and not even pause in my quest to get to the bottom of the Skinny Pop bag. <br><br>PO-TA-TO...PO-TAH-TO<br><br>This coming babble is merely MY way of <s>scrambling</s> explaining how I was okay with this age difference. <br><br>And how that makes me NOT a supporter of pedophilia. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455867903ra/18160136.gif" width="450" height="253" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>PEDOPHILIA</b><br><br>Let's talk about it, shall we? <br><br>Per definition:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Pedophilia or paedophilia is a <u>psychiatric disorder</u> in which an adult or older adolescent experiences a <u>primary or exclusive</u> sexual attraction to prepubescent children."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>In my line of work, I have actually MET convicted pedophiles. (Don't ask, I won't get into it.) But let's just say this... Kellen ISN'T one. <br><br>As it states above, pedophiles experience a PRIMARY sexual attraction to PREPUBESCENT children. They are NOT interested in adults sexually, usually only children - thus the "primary" in that definition. They could "love" a child in their minds, but once that child ages out of whatever their "preferred range" is, that "love" is no longer. <br><br>Now, I'm not saying I would love having a 25 year-old man dating my fictional-hell-hath-truly-frozen-over-13-year old daughter. <br><br>I'm simply saying that Kellen was NOT a fucking sex predator and Wavy his unassuming fairy-child prey. <br><br>He loved <i>WAVY</i>. Regardless of her age. <br><br>Their "situation" was a unique one; thus what made it interesting. <br><br>To me at least, for what that's worth.<br><br>So, if you are on the fence with this one as a result of the age thing - Again, I'm not trying to change the minds of those firmly on one side or the other. This is intended for those in the middle who are unsure if it might bother them or not - To those people I would say to maybe give this one a shot. <br><br><i>After</i> it goes on sale. <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471577478ra/20074796.gif" width="384" height="288" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Because $12.99, homies. <br><br>But back to the book. <br><br>I thought Wavy was a really interesting character. She was quirky and different.<br><br>And she was quirky and different without being Manic Pixie Dream Girl different - which I LOVED.<br><br>GOD, I am sick of that trope. <br><br>Anycliche, back to Wavy. <br><br>I thought she was a really original character who lived a very original story. <br><br>And, even though she had a really shiteous childhood, I appreciated that - while still difficult and believably tragic - Greenwood didn't make it SO over the top tragic that it made me roll my eyes. <br><br>Seriously, that seems to be all the craze these days. Authors seem to think that saddling their characters with all of these heinously tragedy-filled pasts acts as automatic characterization. <br><br>But honestly?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471577478ra/20074797.gif" width="245" height="247" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>All that does is make me roll my eyes and shake my head. <br><br>Another thing I really liked about this story was the layout. <br><br>Every chapter it jumped around to a different narrator and POV. Now, normally this would drive me batshit, but the way Greenwood did it here just really worked for me. <br><br>I thought this format served to give us even more insight into the story and the characters. In some ways, it reminded me a little bit of <i>Nine Minutes</i> in that I felt like Morgan Freeman was reading it to me. <br><br>In my living room.<br>Sitting on my couch. <br>Against the soundtrack of my dog slurping on her ass right next to my face. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471577478ra/20074798.gif" width="480" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>#Yummy<br><br><b>I also really liked the story as a whole and the way that parallels were drawn between Wavy's blatantly abusive mother telling her she was "dirty" and Renee (who to me represented the "norm") being surreptitiously abused in a similar - and yet more socially acceptable manner - by being practically force-fed copious food and then being backhandedly asked seconds later how her diet was going. </b><br><br>Two completely different backgrounds and methods...and yet, kind of abusive all the same, no?<br><br>So, well done, Ms. Greenwood, authoring like this is truly refreshing. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471577478i/20074799._SY540_.jpg" width="250" height="333.5" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now in the same breath that I sound halfway cerebral and semi-fancy...<br><br>...Here comes Shallow Val. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471577479ra/20074800.gif" width="480" height="368" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, I realize that what I am about to say makes me sound heinous and awful. And I am aware of this. <br><br>I'm awful.<br><br>There, I said it for you, so feel free to skip the snark in the comments. <br><br>Or go ahead, I need some amusement. <br><br>But anyshallowend, as I was saying. <br><br>Kellen kept being described as ugly, sweaty, smelly, fat, greasy, I could go on... <br><br>Or I could just leave this quote here:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"I had nothing on my body like the <u>warm damp crease between his tits and belly</u>. Nothing like the muscles that bulged in his arms when he used the pulley in the shop ceiling to hoist engines out of cars."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436545786ra/15475407.gif" width="500" height="239" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm sorry....but...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471577479i/20074801.jpg" width='245"' height="251" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yes, yes, I know what you are thinking. <br><br>"But it's <i>real</i>."<br><br>"It's <i>authentic</i>"<br><br><b>It's <u>MAN TITS</u>.</b><br><br>Now I may be shallow, but I'm not ridiculous. *snort* This didn't factor into my rating or overall love of the book. But - for full transparency - I must say that comments such as these DID pull me out of a few otherwise poignant moments. <br><br>I really enjoyed this story. And while I wouldn't say it is my "top all time read of the year" *dodges projectile objects* it was definitely up there in books I will remember and authors I will keep on my radar. <br><br>And, who knows, I might end up loving it even more later upon further reflection or another re-read. <br><br>Until then, I imagine Wavy standing in an open field, the breeze blowing through her hair, saying:<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>"I could have told him there was no sense in rushing toward being dead. It would find you soon enough, and before it did there were pleasures to make your heart hurt less. If I lay very still in bed at night, I remembered how Grandma's house smelled. The taste of mint ice cream on Kellen's tongue. Donal jumping on the bed to wake me up...."<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471579261i/20074999.jpg" width="400" height="266" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>"...I'm real. I'm as real as you are..."</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br><br>XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX<br><br>Okay, this thing is ALL over my feed. I usually ignore buzz books that I had no independent interest in, but this one has me intrigued now...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471371252ra/20038919.gif" width="500" height="203" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Find me at:<br><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/SteamyReadsBlog/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473872687i/20525702.jpg" width="40" height="40" alt="Follow us on facebook" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.instagram.com/steamyreads/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473872687i/20525703.jpg" width="40" height="40" alt="Follow us on instagram" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="http://www.steamyreads.net" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473872687i/20525705.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_1504758894" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1504758894" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1504758894?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=grit-lit">grit-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1504758894" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6464931543547756620">AND NOW WE ARE BEST FRIENDS WITH SIMILAR TASTE IN B/W GRAPHIC PRINT FASHION!<br/><br/><a href='http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/flat%20stanley003/IMG_2152_zpszdpqefax.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496621326i/22934898._SY540_.jpg' alt=' photo IMG_2152_zpszdpqefax.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>oh, good, i get to be the first reviewer of this book on here. that's not something i usually worry about, but when it's a potentially <i>controvershul</i> book, i get a little leery of being the only target for potential <i>outrage</i>. i had one of the first reviews of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17225311.Tampa' title='Tampa by Alissa Nutting' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tampa</a> on here, too, and i know i'm gonna get a reputation for being totes pro-pedophilia if i keep being such an early cheerleader for these kinds of books, but i</span>
  <span id="freeText6464931543547756620" style="display:none">AND NOW WE ARE BEST FRIENDS WITH SIMILAR TASTE IN B/W GRAPHIC PRINT FASHION!<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/flat%20stanley003/IMG_2152_zpszdpqefax.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496621326i/22934898._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_2152_zpszdpqefax.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>oh, good, i get to be the first reviewer of this book on here. that's not something i usually worry about, but when it's a potentially <i>controvershul</i> book, i get a little leery of being the only target for potential <i>outrage</i>. i had one of the first reviews of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17225311.Tampa" title="Tampa by Alissa Nutting" rel="nofollow noopener">Tampa</a> on here, too, and i know i'm gonna get a reputation for being totes pro-pedophilia if i keep being such an early cheerleader for these kinds of books, but i'll risk it because this book right here is a stunner.<br><br>greg told me i would love it, and here is a reenactment of me reading the back of his copy:<br><br>"blah blah blah meth blah blah blah eight-year-old Wavy blah blah blah tattooed ex-con with a heart of gold blah blah blah powerful and shocking love story wait, <b>WHAT</b>?"<br><br>and i reared back and gave him my closest approximation of the skeptical single raised eyebrow and i said, "love story?" and greg said, "yeah." and i said, "between an eight-year-old girl and a grown-ass man?" and greg said, "yeah, kinda." <br><br>and part of me considered calling the authorities and getting him onto some kind of watchlist, but another part of me was naturally intrigued by an author with these kinda balls. with me, balls always win, so greg remains a free man. for now.<br><br>this is one of those books whose story, if you heard about it on the news or glimpsed some sensationalist headline, would be horrifying, but in THIS book, with THESE characters, where you are privy to interior monologues and backstories and a hundred examples of what defines them as people, it makes sense. it's two damaged people finding something in the other that answers a need, and it's unexpectedly touching. this is not a story told for shock value although it is occasionally shocking, and it should be noted that the book spans fifteen years, and is not <i>quite</i> as disturbing as we all feared, although it still has its moments of readerly discomfort.<br><br>still, it's an incredibly skillful balancing act greenwood pulls off here in terms of addressing the taboo subject matter, which is accomplished by the multiple pov's: half starry-eyed moodlit gloss and half pulling back and looking hard at this relationship from the outside. it's so, so impressive. vibrant. heartbreaking. sympathetic. <br><br>her writing is astonishing. but it's not a matter of description or dialogue or something i could demonstrate by snagging a pull-quote or two; her skill lies in the cumulative, not so much the extractable. she is a pure storyteller who has managed that rare (for me) feat of writing a book that cannot be set down without a little regret. i tend to read at an emotional remove so i crave that feeling of being sucked in and consumed by the power of a story or a landscape; i value immersive storytelling over all other writerly skill sets. if you can suck me in, you win - and this one did that for me - i stayed up until 4:30 reading it that first night and then got up again at 6 to resume, resenting that hour and a half of wasted time. <br><br>it's not perfect - wavy's character is a little unrealistic/inconsistent in her awareness and behavior and the last 1/4 didn't have the same emotional depth or richness as the beginning, so it read a little thin and rushed, but it's a badass powerhouse of a book and i am not here to bitch about the trifling. in fact, i'm rounding this 4 up to a 5 because no one can even stop me, and it was probably a 4.5 in my heart, anyway.<br><br>BOOM.<br><br>plus, maggie likes it:<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/maggie%20on%20books/IMG_6596_zpsorlqajco.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464956139i/19297501._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_6596_zpsorlqajco.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/maggie%20on%20books/IMG_6597_zps7s2wt6vh.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464956139i/19297502._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_6597_zps7s2wt6vh.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>********************************************<br><br><b>congratulations! semifinalist in goodreads' best fiction category 2016!</b><br><br>********************************************<br><br>it's official - coolest author-present ever!! thank you for this, and for writing this book, o bryn greenwood!!<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/flat%20stanley001/IMG_3235_zpsffp65lnq.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464122613i/19200328._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_3235_zpsffp65lnq.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>********************************************<br>review to come. for now -<br><br>WARNING - i came on here to post a status update for this book, but i wanted to make sure i wasn't about to give anything away, so i went to check the synopsis to see how they were handling it, only to find that part is still blank. however, there's a description in the giveaway details - which has a MAJOR spoiler that has not occurred in the book yet and i am on page 208 of a 379 page arc.<br><br>ROONED!<br><br>the book is awesome, so you'll want to enter the giveaway for it but don't go reading any descriptions. just click blindly.<br><br>UPDATE - i added a synopsis to the gr page, so now you don't have to go reading the giveaway synopsis and discovering something that happens around page 230, for goodness' sake.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>

  <span id="freeText14975670782855159117" style="display:none">s<br />st<br />sto<br />stop<br />stop s<br />stop se<br />stop sex<br />stop sexu<br />stop sexua<br />stop sexual<br />stop sexuali<br />stop sexualis<br />stop sexualisi<br />stop sexualsisi<br />stop sexualsisin<br />stop sexualising <br />stop sexualising <b>c </b><br />stop sexualising <b>ch </b><br />stop sexualising <b>chi </b><br />stop sexualising <b>chil </b><br />stop sexualising <b>child </b><br />stop sexualising <b>child </b><br />stop sexualising <b>childr </b><br />stop sexualising <b>childre </b><br />stop sexualising <b>children </b><br />stop sexualising <b>children </b><br />stop sexualising <b>children </b><br />stop sexualising <b>children </b><br /> <i> stop sexualising <b>children </b></i><br /> • stop sexualising <b>children </b><br /> • stop sexualising <b>children </b><br /> <br /><br /> 1: stop sexualising <b>children </b><br />2: stop sexualising <b>children </b><br /> 3: stop sexualising <b>children </b> !!!!!<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><u>have I made my point yet?</u><br /><br />I was just going to quietly mark this as a "no-thanks" and move on but the more I see about it the more I just can't do it. <br />My sister is 16, older then the protag and the thought of her with a 26 year-old is sickening.<br /><br />HERE IS THE THING: Literature does not exist in a void. There is <a href="http://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S1057740801703075" rel="nofollow noopener">alot</a> <a href="http://scholar.google.com.au/scholar_url?url=https://www0.gsb.columbia.edu/mygsb/faculty/research/pubfiles/119/perceived%2520source%2520variability.pdf&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;scisig=AAGBfm1I7QKombRQxgg4ML24dtPnwd1sgw&amp;nossl=1&amp;oi=scholarr&amp;ved=0ahUKEwiSk4bnm4zTAhUHybwKHa9XB64QgAMIGCgAMAA" rel="nofollow noopener">of</a> <a href="https://www.wiwi.europa-uni.de/de/lehrstuhl/fine/mikro/bilder_und_pdf-dateien/WS0910/VLBehEconomics/Ausarbeitungen/MereExposure.pdf" rel="nofollow noopener">research</a> that shows the more we are exposed to something, the more we tend to agree with it. So I'm actually not making this shit up. Too many people are saying this book is okay because it's fiction, and that anyone who has a problem with it just can't make that distinction. Here is an issue: there is no distinction. LITERATURE EFFECTS HOW WE VIEW THE WORLD EVERYDAY. <br /><br />the amount of people saying: this is edgy and pushes the envelope. THIS ISN'T AN ENVELOPE WE NEED PUSHED. We don't need to suggest that pedophilia is maybe ok IT'S NOT. If you want to push an envelope, why not go for something that actually needs pushing??<br /><br />lets push something that actually needs pushing, not the normalisation of pedophilia, which does not. <br /><br />PEDOPHILIA IS NOT OKAY. I really thought that was a basic principle everyone was familiar with but apparently not, not when I have to read with MY OWN TWO EYES the actual words "he is a pedophile and my favourite character of the year"<br /><br />Now, now let me make a distinction. There is a difference between liking a character who does bad things BUT ACKNOWLEDGING THOSE THINGS. For eg, "this villain is a bad person, and he doesn't deserve redemption but he's written really well so I like his characterisation but not his actions" <br />vs<br />"This villain is just misunderstood and what he did isn't that bad he was in a bad situation that caused him to do it I love him"<br /><br />basically: cool motive, still murder. <br /><br />ANYWAY<br /><br />The problem with these books is they normalise and allow pedophilic relationships to be viewed as "okay" and they're not. The problem is people reading this can transfer these beliefs. The problem is not every 13 year old reading this is going to come across a 26 year old as """""nice""""" (I say tentatively but I do understand he didn't pressure for sex), as the 26 year old in this. And 13 year old girls &amp; boys who are very, very vulnerable members of our society deserved to be protected. <br /><br />Excusing pedophilia is not ok. I don't care of Wavy is the most mature 13 year old of all time SHE'S A CHILD. Children cannot make adult decisions, children are at an inherent power disparity to adults and that shouldn't be exploited, children don't deserve to be sexualised just because they may happen to "look adult". They are still !!! children !!!! <br /><br />Anyway, this is my view: this book is gross, and it's problematic, and it's pedophilia. No relationship between a minor and an adult is ever okay <br /><br />bye.</span>

<div id="review_1630730382" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1630730382" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1630730382?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Emily May by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=modern-lit">modern-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=botm">botm</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1630730382" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14428967580674694894"><blockquote>
  <i>Right up until that moment it was sweet and funny. Odd couple that they were, they had a real connection. Then he tugged her boot off and kissed the bottom of her bare foot. I could see him doing that kind of thing to his own kid, but she wasn’t. She was somebody else’s little girl.</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>This book destroyed me.</b> I have never read anything like it. If you know the basic premise - that this is a so-called "love story" between an adult man and a female child - you might be thinking <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7604.Lolita' title='Lolita by Vladimir Nabokov' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lolita</a>! But nah, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114135.All_the_Ugly_and_Wonderful_Things' title='All the Ugly and Wonderful Things by Bryn Greenwood' rel='nofollow noopener'>Al</a></span>
  <span id="freeText14428967580674694894" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Right up until that moment it was sweet and funny. Odd couple that they were, they had a real connection. Then he tugged her boot off and kissed the bottom of her bare foot. I could see him doing that kind of thing to his own kid, but she wasn’t. She was somebody else’s little girl.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>This book destroyed me.</b> I have never read anything like it. If you know the basic premise - that this is a so-called "love story" between an adult man and a female child - you might be thinking <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7604.Lolita" title="Lolita by Vladimir Nabokov" rel="nofollow noopener">Lolita</a>! But nah, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114135.All_the_Ugly_and_Wonderful_Things" title="All the Ugly and Wonderful Things by Bryn Greenwood" rel="nofollow noopener">All the Ugly and Wonderful Things</a> is a completely different beast.<br /><br />Ugly and wonderful really are great descriptors for this story. The best thing about it is the completely unsentimental storytelling that, with its constant switching between perspectives, as well as alternating first and third person, beautifully presents a dark tale of childhood, family and abuse. <br /><br />It's so... not manipulative. The author narrates a series of events, using gorgeous writing, but it's a fantastic example of how <i>showing</i> works so much better than <i>telling</i>. We are never told how to feel. We are allowed to be disgusted, sad and angry on our own terms, and we are allowed to draw our own conclusions about the relationship this book portrays. <br /><br />I came to the end of the novel with my mind reeling, my emotions scattered, and completely unsure exactly what I did feel about it... but one thing is certain: I <i>felt</i>. <b>Oh hell, I felt.</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>She nodded against my arm and after that, we were quiet. We didn’t need to talk. We just laid there watching falling stars go streaking white through all that darkness.</i>
</blockquote><br />The story is about a girl called Wavy and it is a tale that spans around fifteen years. Through the perspectives of Wavy's cousin, brother, teachers and friends, as well as Wavy herself, the story of her childhood emerges as one filled with physical and emotional abuse. Her mother is a drug addict, her father is violent, and her mother's issues with eating and germs manifest in Wavy's behaviour, which, in turn, earns frustration from her teachers and fellow pupils.<br /><br />Then a motorcycle accident brings Kellen into her life. Kellen is a big guy with his own history of abuse at the hands of his father. Called a "fat slob" and generally thought of as a waste of space his whole life, there is an instant connection between these two outsiders. <br /><br />While <b>uncomfortable, disgusting and often graphic</b>, it is so emotionally confusing because Kellen is not another Humbert. His motivations in his relationship with Wavy are loneliness and compassion, and he is not driven by sexual agenda. In fact, Wavy seems somehow removed from the regular notion of sexuality, existing on a plane where she is not an adult or child, male or female, but simply Wavy. Just herself.<br /><br />I'm sure it will provoke many conflicting reactions, but there remains one overwhelming certainty: <b>it's hard to not react passionately to it</b>. Whether you view Wavy and Kellen as two unfortunate victims of their personal circumstances, or as a child being abused by an adult who should know better, their story is a compelling one.<br /><br />Sad and disturbing. I don't think I'll ever get these characters off my mind.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14428967580674694894" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1649226451" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1649226451" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1649226451?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1649226451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10929951513043219810">Let's pretend you have a little sister. Say she is 12 or 13. There's this big older guy she's been hanging out with lately, and you know he's at least 26 years old.<br/>You walk into her room and there she is, on a table, completely naked, legs spread wide, he is sitting there, shirt off, pants open, touching her.<br/>What do you do? What do you think? What do you feel?<br/>That's exactly what I'm feeling reading this. It's not even discomfort any longer. It's shock and pure disgust.<br/><br/>Here are some disturbing qu</span>
  <span id="freeText10929951513043219810" style="display:none">Let's pretend you have a little sister. Say she is 12 or 13. There's this big older guy she's been hanging out with lately, and you know he's at least 26 years old.<br />You walk into her room and there she is, on a table, completely naked, legs spread wide, he is sitting there, shirt off, pants open, touching her.<br />What do you do? What do you think? What do you feel?<br />That's exactly what I'm feeling reading this. It's not even discomfort any longer. It's shock and pure disgust.<br /><br />Here are some disturbing quotes:<br /><br /><i>Three months spending every day in the same room with child molesters and rapists. The whole thing gave me a creeping dread of myself, but I didn't have to lie in the exit interview.</i> Do you still have sexual fantasies about young girls?<i> they asked. No. I never had. I thought about Wavy a hundred times a day, but Wavy was Wavy, not some </i>young girl.<br /><br /><i>"If Wavy showed up tomorrow, I'd do it all over again. I loved her the first time I saw her and I still do."<br />"Love at first sight, huh? How old was she?"<br />"Eight."</i><br /><br /><i>Wavy was almost as small as she'd been at thirteen. She was all long legs and narrow in the hips. Her tits were perfect, but not even big enough to fill my mouth, let alone my hands. She hadn't hardly grown at all. Did it make me a pervert that I still thought she was the most beautiful thing I'd ever seen? Did it make me less of a pervert that twenty and thirteen looked the same on her?</i><br /><br />I think these quotes stand for themselves.<br /><br />A minor sexually involved with an adult is wrong. An adult sexually involved with a minor is a paedophile. No excuses. Full stop. So why is everybody too shy to use this word? Why do I see so many 5 star ratings? Why do people think this is romantic? How can anyone in their right mind approve of this?<br />Yes, this book is beautifully written and utterly compelling. And I hate leaving books unfinished because I feel like I can't judge a book rightfully without reading the last word, which is why I didn't DNF it. But not the most amazing book in the world would set paedophilia right. Not one. So open your eyes. And call it what it is.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/kaispellmeier/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>

<div id="review_1720965687" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1720965687" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1720965687?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2020-audio">2020-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2017-audio">2017-audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1720965687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12213817758540132136"><b>5 stars</b> <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1504991563i/23859067._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>I love out of the box, controversial reads. I love stories that are a bit forbidden and/or on the taboo side. When reviews started coming in for this book I’d never heard of, I knew I had to read it asap. So I picked up the book around 10 pm thinking- I’ll just start it, see how it is. Yeah. I bet you all can guess what happened after that… I stayed up all night reading it. I couldn’t stop even if I wanted to. My eyes were literally burning when I reached 65%, but I carried on. When I f</span>
  <span id="freeText12213817758540132136" style="display:none"><b>5 stars</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1504991563i/23859067._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I love out of the box, controversial reads. I love stories that are a bit forbidden and/or on the taboo side. When reviews started coming in for this book I’d never heard of, I knew I had to read it asap. So I picked up the book around 10 pm thinking- I’ll just start it, see how it is. Yeah. I bet you all can guess what happened after that… I stayed up all night reading it. I couldn’t stop even if I wanted to. My eyes were literally burning when I reached 65%, but I carried on. When I finished, I thought I would crash immediately but I couldn’t sleep. My mind was on Wavy, Kellen, and their story. <br><br>Wavy’s story is not an easy story to read. She grew up with negligent parents and no one who really cared about her. Eight-year-old Wavy keeps to herself and tries to take care of her little brother. But who takes care of Wavy? No one. Until she meets Kellen. Kellen is around twenty when Wavy meets him. Kellen works for Wavy’s father, has tattoos and drives a motorcycle. Kellen becomes the only friend Wavy has and the only person who truly cares for her. Through her neglect and his loneliness, their love blossoms. Don’t get grossed out just yet, when Wavy is a child of 8, it is not a romantic love. Not at all. It’s a true friendship and a real love, without any sex, lust or anything inappropriate. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1504991563i/23859068._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>There were so many POV’s that shaped this story. We don’t just get Wavy and Kellen, we get many side characters. Normally, I don’t love that in a story but it really worked for the way this was told. <br><br>I love reading romance books- it’s my preferred genre. But is this a romance? I guess it is. But it’s more of a love story than true romance if that makes any sense. A lot of this story isn’t romantic and I think that’s what made it so special. The love between these two was beautiful and pure for much of the story and if it started as romance it wouldn’t have worked. This is a couple a rooted for. My heart broke for them both and I wanted nothing more than for them to have each other.<br><br>This is a completely unforgettable read. A truly remarkable read. This author’s writing style captivated me from the start. If you’re looking for a unique and unconventional love story that you won’t be able to put down, this is a must read. I’m sure this won’t be a book that everyone loves, but it worked for me. In fact, it’s a 2016 favorite of mine. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1504991563i/23859069._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="12213817758540132136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16384209-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459720769p2/16384209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1694155789?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>

        rated it

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1694155789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4260945948932769055">Wow! This was a spectacular book. I devoured this story. Beginning to end, I was completely lost in this disturbing, yet beautiful, love story.<br/><br/>While I loved the story, I know that this is a story that many people will not enjoy. There are several difficult and highly controversial topics in this book. I'm pretty open-minded, but even I had a hard time with the relationship turning physical between Wavy (13-14 years old) and Kellen (25 or so years old). As a fictitious story, I was able to come t</span>
  <span id="freeText4260945948932769055" style="display:none">Wow! This was a spectacular book. I devoured this story. Beginning to end, I was completely lost in this disturbing, yet beautiful, love story.<br /><br />While I loved the story, I know that this is a story that many people will not enjoy. There are several difficult and highly controversial topics in this book. I'm pretty open-minded, but even I had a hard time with the relationship turning physical between Wavy (13-14 years old) and Kellen (25 or so years old). As a fictitious story, I was able to come to terms with it eventually. However, in no way would I ever condone that relationship in real life.<br /><br />That being said, the emotions that this book elicited are the reason that I loved it. I was heartbroken, appalled and shocked by Wavy's daily life. As much as I found aspects of their relationship to be unsettling, I could not deny that the love between the two was sincere. <br /><br />Kellen was the only person in Wavy's life that treated her with the slightest bit of compassion and concern. She was the same for him in many ways. These were two lost souls that clung to each other with everything they had.<br /><br />The fact that Kellen was a father-figure, in many ways, to Wavy for so long made accepting their romantic relationship all that much harder for me. It just was unfathomable to me that Kellen would go there. Who does that?<br /><br />Nonetheless, this book blew me away. I love a book that can make me feel the way this one did. I'm still feeling conflicted and uneasy with the content. That being said, I'm still thinking about it, and trying to figure out exactly how I feel, days later. That says a lot. <br /><br />This book will definitely make an impression, be it good or bad. I loved it, but I also hated it at times. If you're looking for an emotional read that will tie you in knots, this is a great choice. It is a tragically beautiful story and completely captivating. This is a phenomenal piece of work and I will definitely be reading future books by this author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4260945948932769055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1551664076" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1551664076" />
    <a title="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys"><img alt="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463498958p2/1053760.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29480865-all-the-ugly-and-wonderful-things">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1551664076" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4338454966087693407">This book won’t be for everyone..and I get that:<br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462985601ra/19069243.gif' alt='Palm Springs commercial photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>My thing is: I read a ton of books. After a while I’m begging for something, anything that is fresh and new. This book is that with big brass balls. <br/><br/>Wavy’s story is not a pretty one. We first meet her when she ends up at her Aunt Brenda’s door. Her mom is in prison, no one can take her, she doesn’t really talk, and she hates to be touched. It’s enough to drive anyone crazy. Brenda can’t deal with Wavy. She sneaks out at night and wanders and Br</span>
  <span id="freeText4338454966087693407" style="display:none">This book won’t be for everyone..and I get that:<br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462985601ra/19069243.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>My thing is: I read a ton of books. After a while I’m begging for something, anything that is fresh and new. This book is that with big brass balls. <br><br>Wavy’s story is not a pretty one. We first meet her when she ends up at her Aunt Brenda’s door. Her mom is in prison, no one can take her, she doesn’t really talk, and she hates to be touched. It’s enough to drive anyone crazy. Brenda can’t deal with Wavy. She sneaks out at night and wanders and Brenda is scared that she will drag her daughters down the wrong road with her. She ends up with Grandma but even that doesn’t last. <br><br>Mom comes to pick her up and now she has a new brother Donal to look after also. They return to their life at the “ranch”. The Ranch is a meth cooking hideout. Her dad Liam is leader of the den. He uses a different woman each time he drops his pants. <br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462985601ra/19069244.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But Wavy’s mom Val is his wife, what time she isn’t lying in filth or stoned out of her mind. She tells Wavy her thoughts on men and food. And passes on her fear of germs. (They will get in you)<br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462985601ra/19069245.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>It’s no wonder Wavy is so messed up.<br><br>Then one day Kellan shows up on his motorcycle bringing them some groceries. He wrecks his motorcycle that day and Wavy gets him help. Kellan is not your typical guy that you imagine a girl looking at twice. He’s big. He’s wooly. He gets told at one point in the story that he needs to use deodorant. But that’s the start of it. Wavy is eight years old. (Not the romance part you pervert-the friendship.)<br><br>I totally saw him as a younger version of this:<br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462985601i/19069246.jpg" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Kellan is one of the only people that Wavy can bring herself to say any words too. They talk about the stars and he just completely understands her. <br><br>As she grows up Kellan stays by her side. He is the person she goes to when she can’t get registered for school because neither of her parents can get their act together to make sure she is going. He stands in when she needs someone. He is the one that protects her. <br><br>The relationship between Wavy and Kellan changes over time. With Wavy there is no questioning. She knows he is the only one for her. Ever. <br><br>Then something bad happens and both their lives are torn apart. I KNOW that those ages of these two should have made me want them to be apart. But fuck that. Who am I to judge someone else’s life? <br><br>Wavy’s life is messed up. Kellan is one of the only good things in the whole thing. I completely rooted for these two characters. <br><br><b>I liked learning things. How numbers worked together to explain the stars. How molecules made the world. All the ugly and wonderful things people had done in the last two thousand years. </b><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462985601ra/19069247.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This book is going on my favorites list. Characters that aren’t cookie cutters. Amazing story-line. Some great writing. If it doesn’t win some kind of award I’m going to be all ticked off because I loved every single word. <br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462985601ra/19069248.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>There was only one thing that was sorta wonky for me in this book and honestly it’s not a biggie because I didn’t even notice until I was half-way though the book. The time period was the late 1970’s and early 1980’s. I don’t remember meth being the drug of choice during that time period. See the thing is…My dad was a drug dealer during that time period. I think this book got into my heart and head so much because some of my past was similar to Wavy’s. I remember being at school and the police officer’s bringing in some drug paraphernalia and it being some of my dad’s stuff. Raids and a fear of the police were nothing new at that house. (Relax-my dad served his time later and my family went even more nuts into religion-but that’s a whole nuther story) My family is a total Jerry Springer wet dream.<br><br>Does that mean that I was in a thing with an older guy? Nope, it means I get where this character is coming from. Real life is not the rich guy sweeping in with his red room. This story is more real life. It’s dark. It’s dirty. Life ain’t always pretty. <br><br> <i>Booksource: Netgalley and St. Martin's Press in exchange for review. THANK YOU!</i><br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462985601i/19069249._SX540_.jpg" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>I read this one with a great group of weirdo's. You can check them out..<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1633165908?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Kelly, </a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1623319600?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Steve,</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1623405561?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Allisa, </a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1635134634?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener"> Dan 2.0,</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1516861005?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Sandra</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1633204188?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Sh3lly</a> <br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="4338454966087693407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1651627512" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1651627512" />
    <a title="Deanna " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15662887-deanna"><img alt="Deanna " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437589889p2/15662887.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1651627512?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deanna " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deanna " href="/user/show/15662887-deanna">Deanna </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15662887-deanna?shelf=highly-recommended">highly-recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15662887-deanna?shelf=my-favorites">my-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1651627512" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4774962612132829766">WOW! I don't even know where to start!! As others have said this book is NOT for everyone. But I was hooked from the moment I started reading.<br/><br/>This book made my head hurt at times as it made me question so many different things. Parts of this book made me very uncomfortable. I honestly felt many different emotions while reading it. Emotional actually doesn't even begin to describe how this book make me feel but it's the first word that comes to mind.<br/><br/>The story and the characters got in my head and</span>
  <span id="freeText4774962612132829766" style="display:none">WOW! I don't even know where to start!! As others have said this book is NOT for everyone. But I was hooked from the moment I started reading.<br /><br />This book made my head hurt at times as it made me question so many different things. Parts of this book made me very uncomfortable. I honestly felt many different emotions while reading it. Emotional actually doesn't even begin to describe how this book make me feel but it's the first word that comes to mind.<br /><br />The story and the characters got in my head and under my skin and I don't see them leaving anytime soon.<br /><br />At first I wondered about the title but honestly, it's perfect for this book.<br /><br />****Possibly some very minor spoilers****<br /><br /><br /><br />The book begins in March of 1975 told from Amy's point of view. Amy is seven when her five year-old cousin Wavonna Quinn (nicknamed Vonnie then Wavy) first comes to live with them.<br /><br />Amy learns a lot about "The Tragic and Edifying Story of Wavonna Quinn" by eavesdropping on her mother when she talks to her book club friends.<br /><br />Wavy hasn't had an easy life so far and seen things that no five-year old should ever have to see. She doesn't talk very much but she's smart as a whip.<br /><br />Thanks to an old neighbor, Wavy can identify all of the stars and constellations. It's one of her favorite things.<br /><br />"Mr. Arsenikos said if you knew the constellations you would never get lost. You could always find your way home."<br /><br />Wavy has some strange habits that drives her Aunt Brenda crazy but endears her to Amy. About six months later, after a late night wandering incident it's decided that Wavy is a danger to her cousins and is sent to live with their Grandmother. We learn more about Wavy's mother Val from Grandma Helen. She explains that nowadays, Val would probably be diagnosed with something, but at the time, they just lived with what they called her "germ problem" along with her other issues.<br /><br />When she first brings Wavy home she realizes how very different her granddaughter is, but she accepts Wavy for who she is and they start to forge a tight bond. I LOVED her grandmother. Sadly, Wavy isn't with Grandma for very long.<br /><br />When her mother is released from prison she tells eight-year-old Wavy that everything is going to be different this time. For two weeks she's "Good Mama" doing the laundry, cooking dinner etc. Then two weeks later Wavy wakes up to "Scary Mama" and realizes that nothing is going to be different. Except now she is not only taking care of herself but also her new baby brother, Donal. Their father, Liam is no real help either. He mostly stays down the hill taking care of his "business" and when he is around Wavy knows to stay out of the way. With Good Mama, Scary Mama, Happy Mama, or Sad Mama we quickly learn why Wavy doesn't talk very often, why she doesn't eat and why she won't let people touch her.<br /><br />One day Wavy is out in the meadow when "A Giant" drives by on his motorcycle. As he turns to look at Wavy he startles and ends up wiping out on the gravel road. Wavy sees something kind in the giant's eyes and tries to help him. He's an ex-con and associate of her father's and his name is Jesse Joe Kellen.<br /><br />Jesse Joe Kellen quickly realizes that Wavy is all on her own with parents who don't seem to give a thought to her care. He quickly becomes everything to Wavy. He buys food, takes her to school and keeps her safe. As time goes by the friendship between this unlikely pair grows into much more.<br /><br />"He smelled good. Sweat and motorcycle and wintergreen. No stinking weed smoke. No perfume. No sadness. He smelled like love"<br /><br />Now this is where many readers may become very uncomfortable. It may make you uneasy at times and horrified at others but at the same time you may not feel like you would normally in this situation. But many readers may find it very hard to wrap their brains around certain parts of this ....love story.<br /><br />We read how Wavy and Kellen view their relationship. But we also get to see how other people feel about it. Not just Wavy's Aunt Brenda and her cousins, but also school teachers, social workers, judges, lawyers, drug dealers, jewelers and many others.<br /><br />This truly is a shocking and powerful book that is controversial and will likely be the topic of a lot of debates. Possibly some very heated debates.<br /><br />Was it all completely realistic? Maybe not. But in the end this is a fiction book and by remembering that it helped me to relax and just appreciate the story. Are my beliefs changed by what I read? Not really. Maybe this sounds strange and I don't really know how to explain what I mean, but I just feel a bit different after reading this.<br /><br />I was so invested in this book, nothing could pull me away (except when my Kindle died and I couldn't find the charger). I couldn't possibly guess how it was going to end. I didn't care that it was four in the morning. I HAD to know what was going to happen next.<br /><br />I am so impressed by this author. There were quite a few characters in this book, and they were all interesting and well developed. I had no problem following the story-line and keeping all of the characters straight. In my opinion the story was fantastic and very well written.<br /><br />So yes, this book may not be for everyone but I'm really glad that I read it and I can't wait to read more from Bryn Greenwood.<br /><br />Thank you to NetGalley and the publisher for the opportunity to read this book in exchange for my honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4774962612132829766" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Mischenko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko"><img alt="Mischenko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587209348p2/1194517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1815125069?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mischenko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mischenko" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko">Mischenko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1194517-mischenko?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1194517-mischenko?shelf=interview">interview</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1815125069" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4744331222903745820">To see this review and a Q&A with the author, please visit <a href='https://readrantrockandroll.wordpress.com/2017/04/28/first-blog-post/' rel='nofollow noopener'>www.readrantrockandroll.com</a><br/><br/><i>All the Ugly and Wonderful Things</i> by Bryn Greenwood is a book that was very challenging for me to read due to the content. The title is nothing short of absolute perfection in describing the book. I went into the book completely blind and didn't read much about it besides liking a few reviews. I had no idea what was in store.<br/><br/>There were a few times in the book I wanted to stop reading. What supported me finishin</span>
  <span id="freeText4744331222903745820" style="display:none">To see this review and a Q&amp;A with the author, please visit <a href="https://readrantrockandroll.wordpress.com/2017/04/28/first-blog-post/" rel="nofollow noopener">www.readrantrockandroll.com</a><br /><br /><i>All the Ugly and Wonderful Things</i> by Bryn Greenwood is a book that was very challenging for me to read due to the content. The title is nothing short of absolute perfection in describing the book. I went into the book completely blind and didn't read much about it besides liking a few reviews. I had no idea what was in store.<br /><br />There were a few times in the book I wanted to stop reading. What supported me finishing the book was reminding myself about the fact that this story, no matter how hard it is to accept, is very real. This is a book of fiction, but there are lives comparable to this and they're very true. Just because they're out of sight, out of mind, doesn't mean they aren't happening. The author could’ve written it differently, but then it wouldn't be what it is. I don't think by reading and finishing the book you're necessarily celebrating the events that take place.<br /><br /><b>**Spoiler**</b><br />The controversy with people is the relationship. I get that the relationship Wavy chooses seems wrong, but just look at her life: her parents, exposure, and experiences are not what most would consider "normal" and she's not able to enjoy her childhood as it is. Instead, she's having to live like an adult and she experiences adult situations at a very young age. Because she doesn’t have anybody— a nonexistent family and no support from anyone —Kellen becomes her family and they fall in love.<br /><br />After all, it's just a story. To me, it was captivating. The book is written very well and I loved it. I'm delighted to have discovered this author and I'm looking forward to reading more. I'll leave it at that. :) <br /><br />5*****</span>
  <a data-text-id="4744331222903745820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1516868292" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1516868292" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528750408p2/9684061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1516868292?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29480865-all-the-ugly-and-wonderful-things">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=emotional">emotional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=mind-fuck">mind-fuck</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1516868292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1085005403895319526"><i>
  <b>“I love you all the way.”</b>
</i> <br/><br/>Never in my life have I read a book that made me feel as uncomfortable as this one managed to. Gritty, raw and wrong on so many levels, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114135.All_the_Ugly_and_Wonderful_Things' title='All the Ugly and Wonderful Things by Bryn Greenwood' rel='nofollow noopener'> All the Ugly and Wonderful Things</a> brought up feelings I wasn’t prepared for.<br/><br/>There were so many times, <b>I wanted to hate this book</b>, to throw it across the room and somehow forget about everything I’d read. Riddled with emotion and a level of constant moral questioning, <b>this story toes the line of pedophilia and begs for acceptance</b>. I</span>
  <span id="freeText1085005403895319526" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“I love you all the way.”</b>
</i> <br /><br />Never in my life have I read a book that made me feel as uncomfortable as this one managed to. Gritty, raw and wrong on so many levels, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114135.All_the_Ugly_and_Wonderful_Things" title="All the Ugly and Wonderful Things by Bryn Greenwood" rel="nofollow noopener"> All the Ugly and Wonderful Things</a> brought up feelings I wasn’t prepared for.<br /><br />There were so many times, <b>I wanted to hate this book</b>, to throw it across the room and somehow forget about everything I’d read. Riddled with emotion and a level of constant moral questioning, <b>this story toes the line of pedophilia and begs for acceptance</b>. It’s the story of a little girl and a grown man falling in love. <br /><br />Even now, there’s a part of me that wants to hang my head in shame because when it really boils down to it, I <i>liked</i> this story. It makes me question, what the fuck is wrong with me? <b>Am I such a sucker for a love story that I’m willing to overlook every repulsive moment</b> between Wavy and Kellan and feel some sort of happiness for the way things turned out, instead? That all of the wonderful things could really wash away the ugly? I guess my answer has to be <i>yes</i>.<br /><br />It’s a guarantee, not everyone will be able to get over the things that feel wrong and dirty. At the end of the day, is it really okay that a little girl fell in love with a grown man and absolutely no one did anything to stop it? No way. Never. Not in a million years. I was utterly disgusted, repulsed and even angry about it. <br /><br />That I managed to get from that point, to the place where I could appreciate the bright spot in the story—two damaged people finding love and acceptance in one another at all costs—should tell you the level of storytelling that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4183574.Bryn_Greenwood" title="Bryn Greenwood" rel="nofollow noopener">Bryn Greenwood</a> pulled off here. <b>Without a doubt, it was the stellar writing that made this so compelling.</b> Not just any author could deliver a controversial topic in such a way that people would feel the need to keep reading and admit they actually enjoyed such a warped and manipulative story.<br /><br /><i>*ARC provided by St. Martin's Press and NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1085005403895319526" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1721116707?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=forbidden-love">forbidden-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family-drama">family-drama</a>,
